or those<br /><br />

for the construction or operation of the Facilities, non-availability of electrical power,<br /><br />

Thisdocument, tie ProgrammeofMiningandMetalTreatmentOperationsforthe<br /><br />
assets that W11 be owned by Konkola Copper Mines PLC (KCM), has been produced to<br /><br />
satisfy the requirements of Part 3 of The Mines And Minerals Act, 1995 in relation to<br /><br />
tie application for a large-scale mining licence. Section<br /><br />
<br /><br />
24 (3) of Part 3 of the Act<br /><br />
<br /><br />
states, inter alia:<br /><br />
a) A comprehensive statement ofthe mineral deposits in the area over which the<br /><br />
licence is sought, including details of all known minerals proved, estimated or<br /><br />
<br /><br />
I<br /><br />
<br /><br />
inferred, ore reserves and mining conditions;<br /><br />
<br /><br />
b) Every application for a large scale mining licence shall include or be<br /><br />
accompanied by the proposed programme ofmining operations, including a<br /><br />
forecast of capital investment, the estimated recovery rate of ore and mineral<br /><br />
products, andthe<br /><br />
<br /><br />
proposed treatmentand<br /><br />
<br /><br />
disposal of ore andminerals<br /><br />
<br /><br />
recovered.<br /><br />
The Progamme of Mining and Metal Treatment Operations for<br /><br />
<br /><br />
t i e KCM assets has<br /><br />
<br /><br />
been based, h general, on t i e Class 1 Feasibility Study that was undertaken by Zambia<br /><br />
CopperInvestmentsLimited (ZCI) inJune1999.Whereveravailable,theFeasibility<br /><br />
Study programme has been updated withmorerecentlyestimatedinformation.The<br /><br />
4<br /><br />

<br /><br />
m pressurisation of the<br /><br />

resulted in inadequate heat dissipation and the slow clearing of fiunes<br /><br />
at blasting times.<br /><br />

New higher duty booster fans will be installed above the production<br /><br />
levels to extract fi-om the workings below and to force the air up the<br /><br />
variousupcastshaftsin<br /><br />
<br /><br />
smes with tie present mainsurface fans.<br /><br />
<br /><br />
This willallow the currentlyinstalledboosterfans<br /><br />

to be removed<br /><br />

m the retum airways andthe<br /><br />

1.1.2 StoDing Methods and Efficiencies<br /><br />
The current mining operation is based mainly on sub level open stopmg<br /><br />
methods (SLOS) using gravity ore flow within stopes where the orebody<br /><br />
.<br /><br />
<br /><br />
.<br /><br />
<br /><br />
-.<br /><br />
-.<br /><br />
<br /><br />
--<br /><br />

~'-iiip~is<br /><br />
s t e q ind iiy scraping~ofh oken ore m flatter dipping StopeS, These<br /><br />
methodshavebeenpractisedextensivelyover<br /><br />
<br /><br />
a numberofyearsat<br /><br />
<br /><br />
Konkola but With variations to suit tie level of mechanisation, mode of<br /><br />
stope drilling, orebody width etc.<br /><br />
3<br /><br />
<br /><br />
The post pillar cut and fill method (PPCF) has been introduced at No<br /><br />
Shaii - using waste rock backfill. SLOS With benching and longitudinal<br /><br />
room and pillar (LW)have also been planned for use in some<br /><br />
No.1 and No.3 Shafts during the interim period<br /><br />
<br /><br />
areas at<br /><br />
<br /><br />
before changing totally to<br /><br />
<br /><br />
the backfill methods for the Konkola Deep Mining Project( K D M P ) .<br /><br />
A temporary backfill plant With a capacity of about 40000m3 per month<br /><br />
<br /><br />
will be built at the existing concentrator and commissioned<br /><br />
<br /><br />
m early 2001.<br /><br />
<br /><br />
Following this, the bulk of the No.3 Shafl stoping will be by the post pillar<br /><br />
cut and fill (PPCF) method.<br /><br />
Twofidlymechanisedtotal<br /><br />
<br /><br />
backfill methods have been planned for<br /><br />
<br /><br />
tie<br /><br />
<br /><br />
KDI'vP. Theseare:<br /><br />
l<br /><br />
<br /><br />
Square excavation level fill (SELF); and<br /><br />
<br /><br />
l<br /><br />
<br /><br />
Post pillar cut and fill (PPCF).<br /><br />
<br /><br />
The K J 3 M P stoping design is based on the following average dilution and<br /><br />
extraction factors:<br /><br />
SELF<br /><br />

PPCF<br /><br />

Thelimitedore reservesremaimngabove 59OmL atNo.3Shaft require<br /><br />
stoping of reserves below that level to commence m about four years time.<br /><br />
To achieve timely dewatering of those reserves, tie 95OmL dewatering<br /><br />
development W11 re-commence after vesting.<br /><br />
The dewatering plan over the thirty year project period is based on tie<br /><br />
WhI., dewateringdevelopmentandthe<br /><br />
extensionoftheexisting<br /><br />
development of the 1 1 5 O m L and 135OmL levels. This has been scheduled<br /><br />
to tie in with theestablishmentofNo. 4 Shaft The development is also<br /><br />
timed to ensure that tie relevant stopes W 1 1 be dewatered before they are<br /><br />
required for production.<br /><br />
TheNo.1Shaft area has moreorereservesthanNo.3<br /><br />
Shaft, a larger<br /><br />
geographical extent to provide for more stoping faces and a higher grade<br /><br />
than thatof No.3 Shaft.Thereforeoutofthetotalundergroundore<br /><br />
production of 2.4mpta, 1.4mtpa will be produced from the No.1 Shafi area<br /><br />
in the early years. No.3 Shaft's production of 1O<br /><br />
. mpta will come fiom a<br /><br />
limited number of stoping faces andby relativelynew methods.<br /><br />
Oreproduction fiom the KDMP resourcescommences m 2004. No.3<br /><br />
Shafl stops hoisting ore in 2005. KDMP production increases rapidly h m<br /><br />
2004 andreachestherate of 6.0mtpa fiom January 2007. Ore hoisting<br /><br />
through No. 1 Shaft closes in 2006.<br /><br />
The temporary backfill plant will remain in operation until the first module<br /><br />
ofthe KDMP backfill plantcomesintooperationinSeptember<br /><br />
2005.<br /><br />
FromSeptember 2005, all stoping will be by backfill methodsand the<br /><br />
second backfill module of the KDMP backfill plant will be commissioned<br /><br />
m April 2006.<br /><br />

A minor expansionwill be made to the existing concentrator during2000 to increase its<br /><br />
<br /><br />
capacity by 20%. The existing concentratorwill be shut down following commissioning<br /><br />
of the new plant m 2005.<br /><br />
The new concentrator, which W11 be positioned approximately three kilometres northwest of the existing concentrator, W11 consist of two 3 million tons per annum modules<br /><br />
that will include mill feed silos, SAG and ball mills, large cell flotation and concentrate<br /><br />
thickening. The thickened concentrate W11 be pumped to tie existing concentrator site<br /><br />
for filtering in a new filterplant.<br /><br />
The flotation tailings W11 be classified m the new backfill plant and the underflow will<br /><br />
be used as the backfill material for the stopmg operations.<br /><br />
1.1.5 Surface Infiastructure<br /><br />
<br /><br />
Most of the surface infhtructure requires general refiu-bishment. Some of the surface<br /><br />
workshop facilities W11 be re-equipped and others will have to be extended to cater for<br /><br />
all of the KDMP requirements. A new changehouse will be required fortie underground<br /><br />
workers to replace the existing changehouse that will have to be demolished to make<br /><br />
way for a major extension to the mainelectrical substation.<br /><br />
The Lubengele tailings dam wall will be raised progressivelyover the thuty years and a<br /><br />
new spillway will be constructed to replace the existing decant tower.<br /><br />

SCHEDULE 2: LOCAL, EUSINESS DEVELOPMENT PLAN<br /><br />
A number of employees have been retrenched recently by ZCCM fiom the assetsthat<br /><br />
<br /><br />
will be owned by KCM. Further retrenchments will be necessary, both before and<br /><br />
after transfer of ownership, to transform the operations fiom the previously overmanned condition toa position where they can become more competitivem terms of<br /><br />
<br /><br />
internationally acceptable productivity performance.h the medium term, certain of<br /><br />
the Nchanga operations will closeas they reach the end of their economc lives. This<br /><br />
will result m additional loss ofjob opportunitiesat the KCM operations.<br /><br />
h years gone by, the direct impact of pastZCCM retrenchment programmes was not<br /><br />
<br /><br />
as obviousas those affected opted, m general, to return to their home districts.<br /><br />
However, more recently, therehas been a significant reversal of this trend and<br /><br />
employees who lose theirjobs now prefer, m the main, to remain resident on the<br /><br />
copperbelt. The recent decision to allow ZCCM employees to purchase their mine<br /><br />
houses will reinforce this tendency. This has resultedm the effects of retrenchment<br /><br />
programmes becoming more localised and with more obvious impact on the general<br /><br />
community m which the mines operate.<br /><br />
Although the current formula used byZCCM to calculate the terminal benefitsis<br /><br />
relatively generousby international standards, it is commonplace m Zambia that the<br /><br />
affected individuals exhaust their cash retrenchment package withina short period. As<br /><br />
most of those affected have no alternative sources ofcash income, they become<br /><br />
L<br /><br />
<br /><br />
increasingly reliant on family support and subsistence farming.<br /><br />
One way of lessening the effects of retrenchment is to encourage and assist the<br /><br />
individuals concerned to establish their own commercial enterprises.K M ,as a<br /><br />
responsible employer,will put into place a programme to facilitate the generation of<br /><br />
these small busmess initiatives.A fidl time facilitator will be appointed by KCM<br /><br />
shortly aftertie-over whose sole task will be to nourish these alternative<br /><br />
opportunities. The facilitator will be experiencedm setting up and managing small<br /><br />
busmess enterprisesand he will be provided with an adequate budget by KCM to<br /><br />
support this ideal. Emphasis will be placed on the development of businessesm which<br /><br />
the ownership is held by Zambian citizens. The facilitator will liaise wth the<br /><br />
<br /><br />
appropriate officials andhe will assist in maintaininga registrar of busmesses m<br /><br />
Zambia that are capable of suppiying materials, equipmentaad services to tie KCM<br /><br />
operations.<br /><br />
The Anglo American Grouphas had a significant success with similar initiatives at its<br /><br />
operations m South Africa and KCM will draw on that experienceto ensure that its<br /><br />
programme achieves sustainable results.<br /><br />
In accordance with Clause5 of the Development Agreement, KCMwill encourage<br /><br />
and assistthe establishment of businesses, particularly on the Copperbelt,to supply<br /><br />
materials, equipment andsemices to KCM.<br /><br />
An interim Local Business Development Programme will<br /><br />
be assembled within six<br /><br />
<br /><br />
months of Closure. A final Local Business Development Programmewill be issued<br /><br />
twelve months after Closure.<br /><br />

SCHEDULE 5: EMPLOYMENT AND DEVELOPMENT PLAN<br /><br />
<br /><br />
It is recognisd that appropriate training and development of the employees is central<br /><br />
to the future success of the KCM operations. To<br /><br />
<br /><br />
that end, priority emphasis will be<br /><br />
<br /><br />
given by KCMto the prowsion of adequate training facilities and the requisite levelof<br /><br />
training skills. These fimdamental prerequisites willbe provided for through adequate<br /><br />
fimding m the operating and capital cost budgets.<br /><br />
<br /><br />
A primary fimction that will be addressed directly after tie-over is a skills needs<br /><br />
analysis across each of the KCM operations. 'Ibis, m turn, will provide a basis on<br /><br />
which the actual details of the training requirement can be assessed and programmed.<br /><br />
The assessment will cover thefull range of training needs fiom the basic requirements<br /><br />
of the semi-skilled employees to the training of supervisors and managers. The main<br /><br />
focus m management and leadership development would be to broaden the scope and<br /><br />
depth of thesecompetenciesatvariouslevelsthroughouttheorganisation.The<br /><br />
s@fics of individualtrainingwilldependon<br /><br />
<br /><br />
a varietyoffactorssuchas<br /><br />
<br /><br />
the<br /><br />
<br /><br />
available potential, existing skills levelsand defined needs.<br /><br />
It is planned that KCM apprentice training will be centred at the Kitwe Trades School<br /><br />
which is included m the KCM assets.<br /><br />
